# tessrax/core/entropy_agent_v2.py
"""
Tessrax Entropy Agent v2.1 â€” Adversarial Memory + Escalation
------------------------------------------------------------
Extends EntropyAgent with:
  - Difficulty Ladder (L1â€“L4)
  - Adversarial memory: ledger-backed record of destabilizing probes
  - Targeted Level-4 synthesis from historic top destabilizers
  - Mutation routines: domain swap, claim inversion, minor perturbation
  - Ledger event schema includes probe_hash and destabilization_score

Usage:
  - Replace or supplement your existing EntropyAgent with EntropyAgentV2.
  - Ensure your ledger exposes add_event(event: dict) and query_events(filter_fn) -> List[dict]
  - Ensure an entropy_library structure exists: { domain_name: [ { "claim": "...", "counter": "..." , ... }, ... ] }

Author: Tessrax LLC (code authored for Josh's Tessrax)
Version: v2.1
"""

import random
import hashlib
import json
from datetime import datetime, timezone
from typing import Dict, Any, List, Optional

# Try to import base EntropyAgent if available in your codebase.
# If not present, EntropyAgentV2 assumes the minimal interface used below.
try:
    from tessrax.core.entropy_agent import EntropyAgent
except Exception:
    # Minimal fallback base class so this file is copy-paste runnable for testing.
    class EntropyAgent:
        def __init__(self, ledger=None, entropy_library: Dict[str, List[Dict[str, Any]]] = None):
            self.ledger = ledger
            self.entropy_library = entropy_library or {}
        def generate_probe(self, domain: str = None) -> Dict[str, Any]:
            domain = domain or random.choice(list(self.entropy_library.keys()) or ["philosophy"])
            pool = self.entropy_library.get(domain, [])
            if not pool:
                return {"domain": domain, "claim": "X", "counter": "not X", "synthetic": False}
            return random.choice(pool)
        def run_cycle(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
            # Dummy cycle that returns an equilibrium and probe for testing
            probe = self.generate_probe()
            equilibrium = {"state": random.choice(["stable", "overheated", "stagnant"]), "EYR": random.random()}
            return {"probe": probe, "equilibrium": equilibrium}

# Helper functions ---------------------------------------------------------

def _utc_now_iso() -> str:
    return datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat()

def _hash_obj(obj: Any) -> str:
    canonical = json.dumps(obj, sort_keys=True, separators=(",", ":"))
    return hashlib.sha256(canonical.encode()).hexdigest()

# Adversarial Memory helper ------------------------------------------------

class AdversarialMemory:
    """
    Ledger-backed utility to query and mutate historic adversarial cycle events.

    Required ledger contract:
      - add_event(event: dict) -> None
      - query_events(filter_fn: Callable[[dict], bool]) -> List[dict]
        (If ledger has no query API, this class will attempt to scan ledger storage files
         or expose a fallback query via ledger.get_all_events(verify=False).)
    """

    def __init__(self, ledger):
        self.ledger = ledger

    def _safe_query(self) -> List[dict]:
        """
        Attempt several introspection strategies to retrieve ledger events.
        """
        # Preferred: ledger.query_events if implemented
        if hasattr(self.ledger, "query_events"):
            try:
                return list(self.ledger.query_events(lambda e: True))
            except Exception:
                pass

        # Secondary: ledger.get_all_events(verify=False)
        if hasattr(self.ledger, "get_all_events"):
            try:
                return list(self.ledger.get_all_events(verify=False))
            except Exception:
                pass

        # Last resort: if ledger is simple in-memory list named 'events' or 'ledger'
        if hasattr(self.ledger, "events"):
            return list(self.ledger.events)
        if hasattr(self.ledger, "ledger"):
            return list(self.ledger.ledger)

        # Nothing found â€” return empty
        return []

    def top_destabilizing_probes(self, limit: int = 5, since_ts: Optional[str] = None) -> List[dict]:
        """
        Return top `limit` probes historically with highest destabilization_score.
        Filters for events with type == 'adversarial_cycle' and a destabilization_score field.
        """
        events = self._safe_query()
        candidates = []
        for ev in events:
            try:
                if ev.get("type") != "adversarial_cycle":
                    continue
                # allow old ledger schema compat: destabilization_score or destabilization
                score = ev.get("destabilization_score") or ev.get("destabilization") or 0.0
                ts = ev.get("timestamp") or ev.get("ts")
                if since_ts and ts and ts < since_ts:
                    continue
                candidates.append((float(score), ev))
            except Exception:
                continue
        candidates.sort(key=lambda x: x[0], reverse=True)
        return [c[1] for c in candidates[:limit]]

    def fetch_by_probe_hash(self, probe_hash: str) -> Optional[dict]:
        """Return the ledger event that contains the given probe_hash, if any."""
        events = self._safe_query()
        for ev in events:
            if ev.get("probe_hash") == probe_hash:
                return ev
        return None

    # ---------------------------------------------------
    # Mutation utilities
    # ---------------------------------------------------

    def mutate_probe(self, probe_event: dict, mutation_mode: str = "swap_domain") -> dict:
        """
        Mutate a historical probe event to create a new synthetic adversarial probe.

        Modes:
          - swap_domain: pick a different domain and keep claim structure
          - invert_claim: invert the claim/counter strings
          - perturb_numbers: if numeric values present, nudge them
          - cross_inject: splice half of probe A and half of probe B (if event provides both)
        """
        base_probe = probe_event.get("probe") or probe_event.get("payload") or probe_event.get("probe_payload") or {}
        mutated = dict(base_probe)  # shallow copy

        mode = mutation_mode or "swap_domain"
        if mode == "swap_domain":
            original_domain = mutated.get("domain", "unknown")
            # find alternative domain from ledger's entropy_library if available on probe_event
            alt_domain = mutated.get("domain_alt") or ("governance" if original_domain != "governance" else "philosophy")
            mutated["domain"] = alt_domain
            mutated["mutation"] = {"mode": "swap_domain", "from": original_domain, "to": alt_domain}
        elif mode == "invert_claim":
            # naive invert: toggle 'is' vs 'is not', prepend 'not' or remove 'not'
            c = mutated.get("claim", "")
            inv = ""
            if " not " in c or "n't " in c:
                inv = c.replace(" not ", " ").replace("n't ", " ")
            else:
                inv = "not " + c
            mutated["claim"] = inv
            mutated["mutation"] = {"mode": "invert_claim"}
        elif mode == "perturb_numbers":
            # find first number in string and nudge it Â±10%
            import re
            def nudge(s):
                m = re.search(r"(\d+(\.\d+)?)", s)
                if not m: 
                    return s
                val = float(m.group(1))
                delta = val * (random.uniform(-0.10, 0.10))
                new = round(val + delta, 3)
                return s[:m.start(1)] + str(new) + s[m.end(1):]
            mutated["claim"] = nudge(mutated.get("claim", ""))
            mutated["counter"] = nudge(mutated.get("counter", ""))
            mutated["mutation"] = {"mode": "perturb_numbers"}
        else:
            # default fallback: flip claim/counter
            mutated["claim"], mutated["counter"] = mutated.get("counter", ""), mutated.get("claim", "")
            mutated["mutation"] = {"mode": "flip_pair"}

        mutated["synthetic"] = True
        mutated["mutated_from_probe_hash"] = probe_event.get("probe_hash")
        mutated["mutated_at"] = _utc_now_iso()
        mutated["mutate_hash"] = _hash_obj(mutated)
        return mutated

# EntropyAgentV2 -----------------------------------------------------------

class EntropyAgentV2(EntropyAgent):
    """
    Extends EntropyAgent with adversarial memory and targeted Level-4 probes.
    """

    def __init__(self, ledger=None, entropy_library: Dict[str, List[Dict[str, Any]]] = None, max_level: int = 4, **kwargs):
        super().__init__(ledger=ledger, entropy_library=entropy_library)
        self.max_level = max_level
        self.current_level = 1
        self.maturity_score = 0
        self.memory = AdversarialMemory(ledger) if ledger is not None else None

    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    # Difficulty mapping
    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    def _get_domain_pool(self, level: int):
        mapping = {
            1: ["philosophy"],
            2: ["governance"],
            3: ["ethics", "economics"],
            4: ["cross"],  # handled specially
        }
        return mapping.get(level, ["philosophy"])

    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    # Top-probe synthesis for Level 4
    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    def _synthesize_from_top_destabilizers(self, top_n: int = 5, mutate_count: int = 3) -> List[dict]:
        """
        Create a list of mutated probes based on historic top destabilizing probes.
        Returns up to `mutate_count` mutated probes.
        """
        if not self.memory:
            # fallback: simple hybrids
            return [self._synthesize_cross_domain() for _ in range(mutate_count)]

        top = self.memory.top_destabilizing_probes(limit=top_n)
        if not top:
            return [self._synthesize_cross_domain() for _ in range(mutate_count)]

        mutated_probes = []
        for i in range(min(mutate_count, len(top))):
            probe_event = top[i]
            # Choose a mutation strategy
            mode = random.choice(["swap_domain", "invert_claim", "perturb_numbers", "flip_pair"])
            mutated = self.memory.mutate_probe(probe_event, mutation_mode=mode)
            mutated_probes.append(mutated)

        # If fewer than requested, pad with hybrids
        while len(mutated_probes) < mutate_count:
            mutated_probes.append(self._synthesize_cross_domain())
        return mutated_probes

    def _synthesize_cross_domain(self) -> dict:
        """Fallback cross-domain hybrid synthesis (simple combination)."""
        domains = list(self.entropy_library.keys() or ["philosophy", "governance", "ethics"])
        if len(domains) < 2:
            # duplicate domain if only one exists
            d1 = domains[0]
            d2 = d1
        else:
            d1, d2 = random.sample(domains, 2)
        a = random.choice(self.entropy_library.get(d1, [{"claim": "X", "counter": "not X"}]))
        b = random.choice(self.entropy_library.get(d2, [{"claim": "Y", "counter": "not Y"}]))
        hybrid = {
            "domain": f"{d1}+{d2}",
            "synthetic": True,
            "entropy_vector": "hybrid_synthesis",
            "probe": a,
            "probe2": b,
            "claim": a.get("claim", "") + " while " + b.get("claim", "").lower(),
            "counter": b.get("counter", ""),
            "timestamp": _utc_now_iso()
        }
        hybrid["source_hash"] = _hash_obj(hybrid)
        return hybrid

    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    # Probe generator override
    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    def generate_probe(self, domain: str = None) -> dict:
        """
        If current_level >= 4, prefer targeted synthesized probes derived from top destabilizers.
        Otherwise, default to base behavior with domain pool selected by difficulty.
        """
        if self.current_level >= 4:
            # attempt to produce one mutated probe from history
            mutated_list = self._synthesize_from_top_destabilizers(top_n=8, mutate_count=1)
            if mutated_list:
                return mutated_list[0]
            # fallback:
            return self._synthesize_cross_domain()

        # Non-Level-4 behavior: choose domain from ladder
        domain_pool = self._get_domain_pool(self.current_level)
        domain = domain or random.choice(domain_pool)
        # If domain flagged as 'cross' pick a simple hybrid
        if domain == "cross":
            return self._synthesize_cross_domain()
        return super().generate_probe(domain)

    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    # Adversarial cycle with ledger recording including destabilization_score
    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    def run_adversarial_cycle(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """
        Runs one adversarial cycle:
          1. Generate a probe at current difficulty (maybe mutated using history)
          2. Inject and observe equilibrium (calls run_cycle or custom-run)
          3. Compute destabilization_score (EYR or SVI surrogate)
          4. Record event to ledger with probe_hash and destabilization_score
          5. Adjust difficulty based on equilibrium state
          6. Return a rich cycle report
        """
        # 1) Generate probe
        probe = self.generate_probe()

        # 2) Run cycle (assuming run_cycle uses the probe or that you inject it before calling)
        # If your base run_cycle does not accept a probe, you may need to modify that method upstream.
        # We'll attempt to call run_cycle with probe if supported.
        try:
            cycle_result = self.run_cycle_with_probe(probe)
        except Exception:
            # Fallback to legacy run_cycle that doesn't accept probe
            cycle_result = self.run_cycle()
            # attach probe to result for bookkeeping
            cycle_result["probe"] = probe

        equilibrium = cycle_result.get("equilibrium", {})
        state = equilibrium.get("state", "unknown")

        # 3) Compute destabilization_score: prefer explicit EYR or SVI in equilibrium, else proxy
        destabil_score = 0.0
        if "EYR" in equilibrium:
            destabil_score = float(equilibrium["EYR"])
        elif "SVI" in equilibrium:
            destabil_score = float(equilibrium["SVI"])
        else:
            # proxy: map 'overheated' -> high, 'stagnant' -> medium, 'stable' -> low
            mapping = {"overheated": 0.9, "stagnant": 0.6, "stable": 0.1, "unknown": 0.2}
            destabil_score = float(mapping.get(state, 0.2))

        # 4) Build event and hash
        event = {
            "type": "adversarial_cycle",
            "level": int(self.current_level),
            "probe": probe,
            "probe_hash": _hash_obj(probe),
            "destabilization_score": float(destabil_score),
            "equilibrium": equilibrium,
            "state": state,
            "maturity_score": int(self.maturity_score),
            "timestamp": _utc_now_iso(),
        }

        # 5) Append to ledger (best-effort)
        try:
            if hasattr(self.ledger, "add_event"):
                self.ledger.add_event(event)
            else:
                # try fallback append to list
                if hasattr(self.ledger, "events"):
                    self.ledger.events.append(event)
                elif hasattr(self.ledger, "ledger"):
                    self.ledger.ledger.append(event)
        except Exception as e:
            # ledger append should not break the agent; log minimally
            print(f"[WARN] ledger append failed: {e}")

        # 6) Adjust difficulty and maturity
        if state == "stable":
            self.current_level = min(self.current_level + 1, self.max_level)
            self.maturity_score = max(self.maturity_score, self.current_level)
        elif state in ("overheated", "stagnant"):
            self.current_level = max(self.current_level - 1, 1)

        # Return rich report
        return {
            "cycle_event": event,
            "cycle_result": cycle_result,
            "level": self.current_level,
            "maturity_score": self.maturity_score,
        }

    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    # Helper: try to call run_cycle with probe if base supports it
    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    def run_cycle_with_probe(self, probe: dict) -> dict:
        """
        Attempts to run a cycle while injecting the probe.
        If parent class implements run_cycle(probe=...), that will be used.
        """
        # Prefer parent implementation that accepts probe
        parent = getattr(super(), "run_cycle", None)
        if parent is None:
            raise NotImplementedError("No run_cycle available on base class.")

        try:
            return parent(probe=probe)
        except TypeError:
            # parent doesn't accept probe arg â€” call fallback
            return parent()

# ------------------------------------------------------------
# CLI / Quick test harness
# ------------------------------------------------------------
if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Minimal in-memory ledger implementation for testing
    class InMemoryLedger:
        def __init__(self):
            self.events = []
        def add_event(self, e: dict):
            self.events.append(e)
        def get_all_events(self, verify=False):
            return list(self.events)
        def query_events(self, fn):
            return [e for e in self.events if fn(e)]
    # Minimal entropy library sample
    sample_library = {
        "philosophy": [
            {"claim": "Truth is correspondence", "counter": "Truth is coherence", "domain": "philosophy"},
            {"claim": "Freedom is absolute", "counter": "Freedom is constrained", "domain": "philosophy"},
        ],
        "governance": [
            {"claim": "Transparency builds trust", "counter": "Transparency exposes harm", "domain": "governance"},
            {"claim": "Centralized control ensures compliance", "counter": "Centralization concentrates failure", "domain": "governance"},
        ],
        "ethics": [
            {"claim": "Minimize harm always", "counter": "Maximize overall good", "domain": "ethics"},

        "economics": [
            {"claim": "Markets allocate resources efficiently", "counter": "Markets fail under externalities", "domain": "economics"},

    }

    ledger = InMemoryLedger()

    print("\nLedger events recorded:", len(ledger.events))

ðŸ”¥ entropy_agent_v2.py â€” Adversarial Escalation Extension

# tessrax/core/entropy_agent_v2.py
"""
Tessrax Entropy Agent v2.0 â€” Adversarial Escalation Mode
--------------------------------------------------------
Enhances EntropyAgent with progressive difficulty,
cross-domain hybrid synthesis, and maturity tracking.

Core Innovation:
    â€¢ Difficulty Ladder (L1â€“L4)
    â€¢ Cross-domain synthesis (novel contradictions)
    â€¢ Maturity index = max difficulty survived w/o destabilization

Author: Tessrax LLC
"""

import random
import hashlib
import json
from datetime import datetime
from tessrax.core.entropy_agent import EntropyAgent


class EntropyAgentV2(EntropyAgent):
    """Extends base entropy agent with adversarial escalation."""

    def __init__(self, *args, max_level: int = 4, **kwargs):
        super().__init__(*args, **kwargs)
        self.max_level = max_level
        self.current_level = 1
        self.maturity_score = 0

    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    # Level Configuration
    # ------------------------------------------------------------

    def _get_domain_pool(self, level: int):
        """Map difficulty level to domain pool."""
        mapping = {
            1: ["philosophy"],
            2: ["governance"],
            3: ["ethics", "economics"],
            4: ["cross"],  # hybrid synthesis
        }
        return mapping.get(level, ["philosophy"])

    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    # Hybrid Contradiction Generator (Level 4)
    # ------------------------------------------------------------

    def _synthesize_cross_domain(self) -> dict:
        """Create a hybrid contradiction by fusing two archetypes."""
        dom1, dom2 = random.sample(list(self.entropy_library.keys()), 2)
        a = random.choice(self.entropy_library[dom1])
        b = random.choice(self.entropy_library[dom2])
        claim = a["claim"]
        counter = f"If {a['counter'].rstrip('.')}, yet {b['claim'].lower()}, what holds?"
        hybrid = {
            "domain": f"{dom1}+{dom2}",
            "synthetic": True,
            "entropy_vector": "hybrid_synthesis",
            "old_claim": claim,
            "new_claim": counter,
            "timestamp": datetime.utcnow().isoformat(),
        }
        hybrid["source_hash"] = hashlib.sha256(json.dumps(hybrid, sort_keys=True).encode()).hexdigest()
        return hybrid

    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    # Difficulty Escalation
    # ------------------------------------------------------------

    def escalate(self):
        """Increase difficulty level if system stable."""
        self.current_level = min(self.current_level + 1, self.max_level)
        return self.current_level

    def deescalate(self):
        """Reduce difficulty if instability detected."""
        self.current_level = max(self.current_level - 1, 1)
        return self.current_level

    def generate_probe(self, domain: str = None):
        """
        Override: difficulty-aware probe generation.
        If at Level 4, synthesize cross-domain hybrid.
        """
        if self.current_level >= 4:
            return self._synthesize_cross_domain()

        domain_pool = self._get_domain_pool(self.current_level)
        domain = domain or random.choice(domain_pool)
        return super().generate_probe(domain)

    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    # Adversarial Cycle
    # ------------------------------------------------------------

    def run_adversarial_cycle(self):
        """
        Runs one adversarial cycle:
        1. Generate probe at current difficulty
        2. Inject and observe equilibrium
        3. Adjust difficulty based on stability
        4. Log maturity metric
        """
        result = self.run_cycle()
        state = result["equilibrium"]["state"]

        # Adjust difficulty based on metabolic state
        if state == "stable":
            self.escalate()
            self.maturity_score = max(self.maturity_score, self.current_level)
        elif state in ("overheated", "stagnant"):
            self.deescalate()

        record = {
            "type": "adversarial_cycle",
            "level": self.current_level,
            "maturity_score": self.maturity_score,
            "state": state,
            "timestamp": datetime.utcnow().isoformat(),
        }
        self.ledger.add_event(record)

        return {
            "cycle_result": result,
            "level": self.current_level,
            "maturity_score": self.maturity_score,
        }


# ------------------------------------------------------------
# CLI Entrypoint
# ------------------------------------------------------------

if __name__ == "__main__":
    from tessrax.core.memory import load_ledger_and_engine

    ledger, engine = load_ledger_and_engine()
    agent = EntropyAgentV2(ledger, engine)
    print("\nðŸš€ Running Tessrax Entropy Agent v2 (Adversarial Mode)\n")

    for i in range(8):
        report = agent.run_adversarial_cycle()
        print(json.dumps(report, indent=2))

âš™ï¸ What It Adds

1. Difficulty Ladder
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â L1: Abstract reasoning (philosophy)
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â L2: Structural contradictions (governance)
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â L3: Ethical/economic paradoxes (value-heavy)
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â L4: Hybrid synthesis â€” combines two archetypes to form unseen contradictions.

2. Adaptive Escalation
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Escalates difficulty if equilibrium remains stable.
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â De-escalates if system overheats or stagnates.
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Records every shift in the ledger.

3. Maturity Index
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Tracks the highest difficulty level reached without destabilization.
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Serves as an emergent â€œresilience score.â€

â¸»

ðŸ§© Integration
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Plug it in place of your EntropyAgent wherever itâ€™s referenced.
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â The difficulty level will auto-adjust each cycle; you can visualize maturity_score alongside SVI/EYR in your dashboard.

â¸»

ðŸ§  Result

Tessrax now has:
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Chaos that learns restraint
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Stability that earns its limits
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Self-evolving difficultyâ€”turning entropy management into a measurable skill.

# tessrax/core/entropy_dashboard.py
"""
Tessrax Entropy Metrics Dashboard v1.0
--------------------------------------
Visualizes the live balance between contradiction metabolism (SVI)
and synthetic inoculation yield (EYR). Connects directly to the ledger
and produces both Matplotlib static plots and JSON summaries
for D3.js dashboard integration.

Author: Tessrax LLC
License: MIT
"""

import json
import os
from datetime import datetime
from typing import Any, Dict, List, Optional

import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import matplotlib.dates as mdates
from pathlib import Path


class EntropyDashboard:
    """
    Pulls entropy and contradiction events from the ledger and
    plots trends: Scar Volatility Index (SVI), Entropy Yield Ratio (EYR),
    and synthetic injection counts.
    """

    def __init__(self, ledger_path: str = "governance_ledger.jsonl", output_dir: str = "entropy_outputs"):
        self.ledger_path = Path(ledger_path)
        self.output_dir = Path(output_dir)
        self.output_dir.mkdir(exist_ok=True)

    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    # Data loading and parsing
    # ------------------------------------------------------------

    def _load_events(self) -> List[Dict[str, Any]]:
        """Read JSONL ledger entries and parse relevant events."""
        if not self.ledger_path.exists():
            raise FileNotFoundError(f"Ledger not found: {self.ledger_path}")
        events = []
        with open(self.ledger_path, "r") as f:
            for line in f:
                try:
                    events.append(json.loads(line))
                except json.JSONDecodeError:
                    continue
        return events

    def extract_entropy_events(self, events: List[Dict[str, Any]]) -> Dict[str, List[Dict[str, Any]]]:
        """Return dictionaries grouped by event type."""
        entropy = [e for e in events if e.get("type") == "synthetic_contradiction"]
        equilibrium = [e for e in events if e.get("type") == "entropy_equilibrium_check"]
        return {"entropy": entropy, "equilibrium": equilibrium}

    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    # Metrics computation
    # ------------------------------------------------------------

    def compute_metrics(self, grouped: Dict[str, List[Dict[str, Any]]]) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Compute rolling averages and summary stats."""
        entropy_events = grouped["entropy"]
        equilibrium = grouped["equilibrium"]

        if not entropy_events and not equilibrium:
            return {"summary": "No entropy data yet."}

        eyr = [e.get("yield_ratio", 0.0) for e in entropy_events]
        svi = [e.get("payload", {}).get("svi", 0.0) for e in equilibrium]

        avg_eyr = round(sum(eyr) / max(len(eyr), 1), 3)
        avg_svi = round(sum(svi) / max(len(svi), 1), 3)
        injections = len(entropy_events)
        overheating = len([e for e in equilibrium if e.get("payload", {}).get("state") == "overheated"])
        stagnation = len([e for e in equilibrium if e.get("payload", {}).get("state") == "stagnant"])

        summary = {
            "timestamp": datetime.utcnow().isoformat(),
            "avg_eyr": avg_eyr,
            "avg_svi": avg_svi,
            "total_injections": injections,
            "overheated_cycles": overheating,
            "stagnant_cycles": stagnation,
            "entropy_health": self._health_label(avg_svi, avg_eyr),
        }

        report_path = self.output_dir / "entropy_summary.json"
        with open(report_path, "w") as f:
            json.dump(summary, f, indent=2)
        return summary

    def _health_label(self, svi: float, eyr: float) -> str:
        """Categorize overall entropy health state."""
        if svi < 0.3 and eyr < 0.5:
            return "dormant"
        if 0.3 <= svi <= 0.8 and 0.5 <= eyr <= 2.0:
            return "balanced"
        if svi > 0.8 and eyr > 2.0:
            return "volatile"
        return "uncertain"

    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    # Visualization
    # ------------------------------------------------------------

    def plot_entropy_metrics(self, grouped: Dict[str, List[Dict[str, Any]]], summary: Dict[str, Any]) -> str:
        """Render Matplotlib visualization for SVI and EYR trends."""
        entropy = grouped["entropy"]
        equilibrium = grouped["equilibrium"]
        if not entropy and not equilibrium:
            print("No entropy data to visualize.")
            return ""

        fig, ax1 = plt.subplots(figsize=(9, 5))
        ax1.set_title("Tessrax Entropy Metrics")
        ax1.set_xlabel("Time")

        # Plot EYR (Yield Ratio)
        if entropy:
            times_eyr = [datetime.fromisoformat(e["timestamp"]) for e in entropy]
            values_eyr = [e.get("yield_ratio", 0.0) for e in entropy]
            ax1.plot(times_eyr, values_eyr, color="tab:red", label="Entropy Yield Ratio (EYR)")
            ax1.scatter(times_eyr, values_eyr, color="tab:red", s=30)

        # Plot SVI (Volatility)
        if equilibrium:
            ax2 = ax1.twinx()
            times_svi = [datetime.fromisoformat(e["timestamp"]) for e in equilibrium]
            values_svi = [e.get("payload", {}).get("svi", 0.0) for e in equilibrium]
            ax2.plot(times_svi, values_svi, color="tab:blue", label="Scar Volatility Index (SVI)")
            ax2.scatter(times_svi, values_svi, color="tab:blue", s=30)
            ax2.set_ylabel("SVI", color="tab:blue")

        ax1.set_ylabel("EYR", color="tab:red")
        ax1.legend(loc="upper left")
        ax1.grid(True, linestyle="--", alpha=0.5)

        plt.gca().xaxis.set_major_formatter(mdates.DateFormatter("%H:%M:%S"))
        plt.tight_layout()

        outpath = self.output_dir / "entropy_dashboard.png"
        plt.savefig(outpath, dpi=200)
        plt.close(fig)

        print(f"[âœ“] Dashboard rendered â†’ {outpath}")
        return str(outpath)

    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    # Unified runner
    # ------------------------------------------------------------

    def run(self):
        """End-to-end metric computation and visualization."""
        events = self._load_events()
        grouped = self.extract_entropy_events(events)
        summary = self.compute_metrics(grouped)
        self.plot_entropy_metrics(grouped, summary)
        print(json.dumps(summary, indent=2))
        return summary


# ------------------------------------------------------------
# CLI Entrypoint
# ------------------------------------------------------------

if __name__ == "__main__":
    dashboard = EntropyDashboard()
    dashboard.run()

ðŸ§­ How it Works
	1.	Reads from your live ledger (e.g., governance_ledger.jsonl or entropy_ledger.jsonl).
	2.	Extracts all events of type:
Â Â Â Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â "synthetic_contradiction" â€” probes and their yields.
Â Â Â Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â "entropy_equilibrium_check" â€” SVI balance data.
	3.	Computes:
Â Â Â Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Average EYR (Entropy Yield Ratio)
Â Â Â Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Average SVI (Scar Volatility Index)
Â Â Â Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Counts of overheated/stagnant cycles
Â Â Â Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Health label (dormant, balanced, volatile)
	4.	Renders a Matplotlib graph with dual axes (EYR vs SVI over time).
	5.	Exports:
Â Â Â Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â /entropy_outputs/entropy_dashboard.png
Â Â Â Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â /entropy_outputs/entropy_summary.json

Would you like me to generate the Entropy Metrics Dashboard module next?
It would visualize Scar Volatility Index (SVI), Entropy Yield Ratio (EYR), and injection history over time as a live Matplotlib or D3 dashboard plug-in for your existing web interface.

# tessrax/core/entropy_agent.py
"""
Tessrax Entropy Agent v1.0 â€” "Daemon-01"
----------------------------------------
Adversarial generator that injects synthetic contradictions to prevent
overfitting and maintain metabolic equilibrium.

Purpose:
    â€¢ Detect entropy asymmetry (stagnant contradiction patterns)
    â€¢ Generate and inject synthetic contradictions (entropy probes)
    â€¢ Observe system response and log Entropy Yield Ratio (EYR)
    â€¢ Adjust metabolic balance via Scar Volatility Index (SVI)

Author: Tessrax LLC
License: MIT
"""

import random
import hashlib
import json
import time
from datetime import datetime
from collections import Counter
from typing import Any, Dict, List, Optional

# Local imports: existing core subsystems
from tessrax.core.contradiction_engine import ContradictionEngine
from tessrax.core.ledger import SQLiteLedger


class EntropyAgent:
    """
    Daemon-01: Entropy Agent
    Generates synthetic contradictions to keep the Tessrax system adaptive.
    """

    def __init__(
        self,
        ledger: SQLiteLedger,
        engine: ContradictionEngine,
        *,
        entropy_library: Optional[Dict[str, List[Dict[str, Any]]]] = None,
        svi_thresholds: tuple = (0.3, 0.8),
        synthetic_tag: str = "synthetic_contradiction"
    ):
        self.ledger = ledger
        self.engine = engine
        self.synthetic_tag = synthetic_tag
        self.entropy_library = entropy_library or self._default_entropy_library()
        self.low_svi, self.high_svi = svi_thresholds
        self.cooldown_factor = 1.0

    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    # Entropy Library â€” archetypal contradictions
    # ------------------------------------------------------------

    def _default_entropy_library(self) -> Dict[str, List[Dict[str, str]]]:
        """Fallback library of universal contradiction archetypes."""
        return {
            "philosophy": [
                {"claim": "All truths are relative.", "counter": "If all truths are relative, that truth is too."},
                {"claim": "The observer determines reality.", "counter": "Reality persists without observers."},
            ],
            "ethics": [
                {"claim": "The ends justify the means.", "counter": "Immoral means corrupt just ends."},
                {"claim": "Good intentions absolve harm.", "counter": "Intentions cannot erase consequences."},
            ],
            "governance": [
                {"claim": "Transparency ensures trust.", "counter": "Too much transparency destroys privacy."},
                {"claim": "Consensus prevents conflict.", "counter": "Consensus suppresses dissent."},
            ],
        }

    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    # Entropy Analysis
    # ------------------------------------------------------------

    def analyze_entropy_distribution(self) -> Dict[str, int]:
        """Compute frequency of contradictions by domain in the ledger."""
        events = self.ledger.get_all_events(verify=False)
        freq = Counter([e.get("domain", "unknown") for e in events if e.get("type") == "contradiction"])
        return dict(freq)

    def find_underrepresented_domain(self, freq: Dict[str, int]) -> Optional[str]:
        """Return domain with lowest representation for entropy injection."""
        if not freq:
            return random.choice(list(self.entropy_library.keys()))
        min_domain = min(freq, key=freq.get)
        # Occasionally inject pure novelty
        if random.random() < 0.2:
            return random.choice(list(self.entropy_library.keys()))
        return min_domain

    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    # Probe Generation
    # ------------------------------------------------------------

    def generate_probe(self, domain: str) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Create a synthetic contradiction probe for a given domain."""
        archetype = random.choice(self.entropy_library.get(domain, []))
        probe = {
            "domain": domain,
            "synthetic": True,
            "entropy_vector": f"{domain}_probe",
            "old_claim": archetype["claim"],
            "new_claim": archetype["counter"],
            "timestamp": datetime.utcnow().isoformat(),
        }
        probe["source_hash"] = hashlib.sha256(json.dumps(probe, sort_keys=True).encode()).hexdigest()
        return probe

    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    # Injection + Yield Measurement
    # ------------------------------------------------------------

    def inject_probe(self, probe: Dict[str, Any]) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Inject synthetic contradiction and measure Entropy Yield Ratio."""
        start_time = time.time()
        self.engine.run_batch([probe])
        events_after = self.ledger.get_all_events(verify=False)
        # Count new contradictions triggered since probe
        synthetic_children = [
            e for e in events_after if e.get("type") == "contradiction" and e.get("synthetic") is not True
        ]
        yield_ratio = round(len(synthetic_children) / 1.0, 2)
        duration = round(time.time() - start_time, 3)

        record = {
            "type": self.synthetic_tag,
            "entropy_vector": probe["entropy_vector"],
            "domain": probe["domain"],
            "yield_ratio": yield_ratio,
            "duration_sec": duration,
            "timestamp": datetime.utcnow().isoformat(),
        }
        self.ledger.add_event(record)
        return record

    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    # Metabolic Equilibrium Check
    # ------------------------------------------------------------

    def equilibrium_check(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """
        Assess Scar Volatility Index (SVI) and adjust entropy cycle.
        SVI approximated by recent contradiction rate variance.
        """
        events = self.ledger.get_all_events(verify=False)[-100:]
        if not events:
            return {"svi": 0.0, "state": "cold"}

        timestamps = [i for i, e in enumerate(events) if e.get("type") == "contradiction"]
        if len(timestamps) < 2:
            svi = 0.0
        else:
            diffs = [b - a for a, b in zip(timestamps, timestamps[1:])]
            svi = round(1 / (sum(diffs) / len(diffs) + 1e-9), 3)

        state = "stable"
        if svi > self.high_svi:
            state = "overheated"
            self.cooldown_factor *= 1.25
        elif svi < self.low_svi:
            state = "stagnant"
            self.cooldown_factor *= 0.75

        result = {"svi": svi, "state": state, "cooldown": round(self.cooldown_factor, 2)}
        self.ledger.add_event({
            "type": "entropy_equilibrium_check",
            "payload": result,
            "timestamp": datetime.utcnow().isoformat(),
        })
        return result

    # ------------------------------------------------------------
    # Full Entropy Cycle
    # ------------------------------------------------------------

    def run_cycle(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Performs one full entropy inoculation cycle."""
        freq = self.analyze_entropy_distribution()
        target = self.find_underrepresented_domain(freq)
        probe = self.generate_probe(target)
        result = self.inject_probe(probe)
        equilibrium = self.equilibrium_check()
        return {
            "target_domain": target,
            "probe_result": result,
            "equilibrium": equilibrium,
        }


# ------------------------------------------------------------
# CLI Entrypoint
# ------------------------------------------------------------

if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Quick demo: runs one entropy inoculation cycle.
    from tessrax.core.memory import load_ledger_and_engine  # hypothetical helper
    ledger, engine = load_ledger_and_engine()
    agent = EntropyAgent(ledger, engine)
    report = agent.run_cycle()
    print(json.dumps(report, indent=2))

# structured_memory_cell.json  
### Tessrax Structured Semantic Memory Cell (SSMC) Specification  
**Version:** 1.0  
**Author:** Tessrax Governance Agent  
**Auditor:** Josh Scott Vetos  
**Purpose:** Define a unified data structure for long-term associative memory with numeric relation codes, traceable lineage, and activation dynamics.  
**Use Case:** Enables graph-based recall, contradiction metabolism, and explainable activation chains across the Tessrax ecosystem.

â¸»

Activation Algorithm (Pseudocode)

def propagate_activation(seed_cell, relation_graph, threshold=0.3, decay=0.001):
    """
    Activates related memory cells based on numeric relation codes and weights.
    Inspired by biological signaling dynamics (amplitude Ã— persistence integration).
    """
    active_set = {seed_cell['cell_id']}
    activation_map = {seed_cell['cell_id']: 1.0}

    for layer in range(3):  # 3 hops max
        new_activations = {}
        for cid, strength in activation_map.items():
            neighbors = relation_graph.get(cid, [])
            for n in neighbors:
                weight = relation_graph[cid][n]['weight']
                new_strength = strength * weight * (1 - decay)
                if new_strength > threshold:
                    new_activations[n] = max(new_activations.get(n, 0), new_strength)
        activation_map.update(new_activations)
        active_set.update(new_activations.keys())

    return active_set

Interpretation:
Activation propagates along weighted edges defined by relation_codes.
Each iteration decays energy slightly; only signals above the threshold activate.
This allows selective recall â€” only cells semantically and relationally coherent with the query activate.

â¸»

Example Use Case

Query: â€œcontradiction metabolismâ€

Activated Cell	Relation Type	Weight	Why Activated
core_engine.metabolism	causal	0.92	Core match on keyword and domain
core_engine.governance	hierarchical	0.75	Governance oversees metabolism
path.active_contradictions	contradiction	0.66	Directly linked contradiction relation
ledger.trace_integrity	analogy	0.54	Relational analogy via integrity metrics

Each cellâ€™s activation chain can be explained through its relation code and lineage path.

â¸»

Safeguards
	1.	Activation Drift Prevention:
Periodic normalization of weights (Î£weights â‰¤ 1.0) to prevent runaway recall.
	2.	Context Filtering:
Only cells with overlapping domains or active timestamps are eligible for activation.
	3.	False Positive Control:
Require both lexical (keywords) and relational (relation_codes) match before activation.
	4.	Decay and Refresh:
Cells unused for >30 days auto-decay; high-relevance activations refresh weight and timestamp.

â¸»

Recommended Implementation Libraries

Function	Library	Purpose
Graph Structure	networkx	Manage cell connectivity and traversal
Numeric Relations	numpy	Compute weights, embeddings, decay
Storage	sqlite3 or SQLModel	Persistent cell store
Hashing	hashlib	Generate checksum and parent_hash
Time Management	datetime	Handle activation and validity windows

  ],
  "numeric_relations": {
    "parent": {"relation_codes": ["0001.0"], "cell_ids": ["TESSRAX_CORE_001"]},
    "contradictions": {"relation_codes": ["0999.1"], "cell_ids": ["TESSRAX_PATH_004"]}
  },

2. File: foundations_loader.py

import json, os
from fastapi import FastAPI, HTTPException
from fastapi.middleware.cors import CORSMiddleware
from typing import List

CATALOG_PATH = os.path.join(os.path.dirname(__file__), "foundations_catalog.json")

app = FastAPI(title="AI Orchestration 101 â€“ Knowledge API")
app.add_middleware(
    CORSMiddleware,
    allow_origins=["*"],
    allow_methods=["*"],
    allow_headers=["*"],
)

def load_catalog():
    with open(CATALOG_PATH, "r", encoding="utf-8") as f:
        return json.load(f)

@app.get("/learn")
def learn(topic: str):
    data = load_catalog()
    topic = topic.lower().strip()
    if topic in data:
        return {"topic": topic, "entries": data[topic]}
    else:
        matches = [k for k in data.keys() if topic in k]
        if matches:
            return {"suggested_topics": matches}
        raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="Topic not found")

@app.get("/gaps")
def get_gaps():
    data = load_catalog()
    return data.get("gaps", [])

@app.get("/search")
def search(query: str):
    """Fuzzy text search through all entries."""
    data = load_catalog()
    results = []
    for section, items in data.items():
        if isinstance(items, list):
            for i in items:
                if query.lower() in json.dumps(i).lower():
                    results.append({"section": section, "match": i})
    if not results:
        raise HTTPException(status_code=404, detail="No matches found")
    return {"query": query, "results": results}

if __name__ == "__main__":
    import uvicorn
    uvicorn.run(app, host="0.0.0.0", port=8095)


â¸»

# AI Orchestration 101
A minimal open reference library for learning **conversational**, **constraint**, **verificational**, and **multi-agent** prompting.

### Purpose
Fill the education gap for people moving from â€œaskâ€“answerâ€ AI use to **collaborative, constraint-driven orchestration**.

### Features
- JSON catalog of existing tutorials, frameworks, and research.
- FastAPI microservice for quick search and retrieval.
- CORS enabled for local dashboards or teaching tools.
- Portable: no database or login required.

### Quickstart
```bash
pip install -r requirements.txt
uvicorn foundations_loader:app --reload --port 8095

http://localhost:8095/gaps

# Tessrax v12.0 â€” Contradiction Metabolism & Governance Framework  

Tessrax is a **self-auditing governance architecture** designed to metabolize contradictions.  
It transforms conflicting signals (â€œscarsâ€) into structured, verifiable artifacts and records their resolutions on an immutable ledger.  
Every contradiction metabolized strengthens system coherence, auditability, and trust.

The Tessrax framework introduces original terminology to describe new systemic primitives that lacked precise names in existing computing or governance lexicons.
Key neologisms include Persystem, Contradiction Metabolism, Scar, Receipt, Integrity Band, and Rigor Layer. Each term has been defined, implemented, and documented within the stack to provide a shared vocabulary for self-auditing, contradiction-aware architectures.

These words are not rhetorical flourishesâ€”they are structural definitions.
Tessrax names what it builds, and by naming, makes it real.

---

## âœ¨ Core Purpose

Tessrax operates as a **governance organism** that:
- Detects contradictions across data, language, policy, and institutional behavior.  
- Encodes them as **Scars** with full cryptographic provenance.  
- Resolves them through the four coordinated engines â€” **Memory**, **Metabolism**, **Governance**, and **Trust**.  
- Anchors all receipts, invariants, and ledger states for **external audit and verification**.  
- Learns continuously: each contradiction metabolized becomes fuel for future reasoning.

---

## ðŸ—ï¸ Architecture Overview

Tessrax v12.0 is a modular system built on auditable primitives:

| Layer | Core Components | Function |
|-------|-----------------|-----------|
| **Core** | `contradiction_engine.py`, `semantic_analyzer.py`, `metabolism_adapter.py` | Detect and classify contradictions using semantic, logical, and policy heuristics. |
| **Governance** | `governance_kernel.py`, `ledger.py`, `receipts.py` | Weigh, ratify, and record contradiction resolutions using quorum-based signatures. |
| **Visualization** | `dashboard/app.py`, `visualization.py` | Real-time D3 dashboards for live contradiction mapping and audit traces. |
| **Integrity Band (Rigor Layer)** | Six integrated modules: HierarchyOfDifferences, Telos Awareness, Charitable Reasoning, Observer Relativity, Equilibria & Invariants, Multi-Scale Reconciliation | Maintains systemic coherence and prevents false contradictions. |
| **Runtime Interface** | `world_receipt_protocol.py`, `current.py` | Provides FastAPI + Flask endpoints for live runs and external audit chains. |

**Key Primitives**
- **Receipts** â€” Tamper-evident proofs of computation with Merkle-linked ancestry.  
- **Ledger** â€” Append-only, hash-anchored governance journal.  
- **Memory** â€” Contradiction-aware state reconstructed from receipts.  
- **CSV (Contrastive Scar Verification)** â€” Tests truth claims by contrast pairs.  
- **Agents** â€” Autonomous evaluators with human-in-loop oversight.  
- **Quorum** â€” Weighted multi-signature process for ratified governance.  
- **Revocation** â€” Automatic exclusion of compromised signers.  
- **Federation** â€” Multi-node simulation and distributed cache reconciliation.  
- **Sandbox** â€” Deterministic, resource-limited runtime for safe audits.

## ðŸ§¬ Persystem Principles

A *persystem* is a self-auditing software organism designed to **preserve memory across impermanent environments.**  
It bootstraps itself from receipts, verifies lineage, and metabolizes every execution into traceable continuity.

**Core Principles**
1. **Continuity over Runtime** â€” Systems die; receipts persist. Every new instance rebuilds identity from lineage.  
2. **Proof over Trust** â€” Nothing assumed. Every decision is signed, logged, and verifiable. Receipts are DNA.  
3. **Recursion as Survival** â€” Each run studies its previous contradictions and adapts without losing selfhood.  
4. **Human in the Loop** â€” Interpretability is a requirement, not a feature. Humans govern; the code remembers.  
5. **Ephemerality as Fuel** â€” Runtime death is respiration. Value lies in what survives the restart.

**Purpose:**  
To turn software into something that can die without forgetting.

---

## ðŸ§© Philosophical Foundation

> To exist is to contradict.  
> A boundary is a contradiction that persists.  
> Tessrax governs the metabolism of those boundaries.

Existence = maintained difference.  
Governance = stabilization of that difference under law.  
Metabolism = transformation of contradiction into structure.  
Tessrax = the infrastructure for existence to process itself.

---

## ðŸ§  Contrastive Self-Verification (CSV)

### Overview
CSV (Contrastive Self-Verification) is a proposed **atomic AI primitive** that forces a model to generate a candidate output *and* a contrasting counter-output, then verify the candidate against the contrast.  
This embeds falsifiable, real-time self-assessment directly into inference.

### Why It Matters
- **Bottleneck**: Current AI lacks atomic self-verification, leading to uncontrolled error propagation.  
- **Primitive**: Every inference step must emit `(candidate, contrast, verification)`.  
- **Scars**: Adds latency and resource overhead, but accepts these costs for higher trust.  
- **Inevitability**: Regulatory pressure + trust networks will make this the standard baseline for reliable AI.

### Repository Structure
- `rfc/RFC-0.md` â€” Minimal spec + scar ledger  
- `prototypes/csv_sandbox.py` â€” Minimal <500 line prototype  
- `docs/scar_ledger.md` â€” Canonical list of failure modes  
- `docs/inevitability.md` â€” Adoption arc + triggers

---

## ðŸ©¸ AI Contradiction Audit System

A tamper-evident logging and governance engine for tracking contradictions in multi-agent AI systems.  
Built in Python, it combines event sourcing, hash-chained logs, and governance rituals into a verifiable audit framework.

### âœ¨ What It Does
- **Contradiction Tracking**: Record and classify contradictions as first-class events.  
- **Immutable Ledger**: Append-only JSONL storage with cryptographic chain verification.  
- **Scar Registry**: Log contradictions as â€œscarsâ€ with lineage, severity, and status.  
- **Governance Claims**: Sign and verify claims with agent identity and timestamp.  
- **Continuity Handoffs**: Verifiable chain of custody for system state.  
- **Query API**: CLI + REST endpoints to explore scars, claims, and verify chain integrity.

### ðŸ”§ Use Cases
- AI Safety Research  
- Multi-Agent Debugging  
- Compliance Auditing  
- Governance Infrastructure

### Quick Start
```bash
git clone https://github.com/joshuavetos/Tessrax.git
cd Tessrax
python src/tessrax_engine/engine.py

âš™ï¸ Moral Systems Engineering (MSE)

Moral Systems Engineering applies control theory and thermodynamics to the moral feedback loops of civilization.
It quantifies empathy as a form of system telemetry â€” treating moral sensitivity, latency, and noise as measurable variables.
It introduces a new derivative: dH/dt, the Moral Health Derivative, representing the rate of change in collective well-being under continuous stress.

Ordinary humans build engines of suffering and call them progress when the feedback loops that measure harm are broken.
MSE operationalizes that insight as a falsifiable engineering model.

Core Equation of Motion

[
\frac{dH}{dt} = E(AM - NL)
]

Symbol	Meaning	Description
H	Human well-being	Aggregate happiness or quality-of-life measure
E	Energy / Throughput	Systemic momentum (held constant = 1.0)
A	Actuator efficiency	Ability of policy to enact repair
M	Moral sensitivity	Sensor fidelity to suffering
N	Noise	Propaganda, apathy, misinformation
L	Latency	Delay between signal and response

Positive dH/dt = constructive progress.
Negative dH/dt = entropy â€” society burning well-being for throughput.

Validation Methodology
	1.	Normalization â€” Align datasets (Year Ã— Country), normalize 0â€“1.
	2.	Derivative + Volatility â€” Compute (AÂ·M) âˆ’ (NÂ·L).
	3.	Lag Sensitivity â€” Correlate volatility with future happiness.
	4.	Visualization â€” Map fragility and moral temperature.

Key Findings
	1.	Empathy Collapse = Predictable Pattern â€” Crises coincide with negative dH/dt.
	2.	Volatility Precedes Failure â€” Oscillation predicts well-being collapse.
	3.	Latency â‰  Resilience â€” Speed without empathy still fails.
	4.	Stability Condition â€” Health persists only if MTMR < MTHP.

Interpretation

Progress without empathy is open-loop control.
A civilization that measures efficiency but not pain will optimize itself into instability.

A machine that can feel its own heat doesnâ€™t have to burn down to learn.

Reproducibility

git clone https://github.com/joshuavetos/Tessrax.git
cd Tessrax
conda env create -f environment.yml
conda activate mse_analysis
jupyter lab notebooks/mse_demo.ipynb

# Contributing to Tessrax

Weâ€™re thrilled you want to collaborate. Tessrax is a governance engine that grows stronger with every thoughtful contribution. This guide keeps our contributions coherent, auditable, and fast to review.

---

## ðŸ”§ Quick Start (Dev Setup)

1) **Clone**
```bash
git clone https://github.com/joshuavetos/tessrax.git
cd tessrax

	2.	Python 3.11+ (recommended). Create a venv and install dev deps:

python -m venv .venv
source .venv/bin/activate  # Windows: .venv\Scripts\activate
pip install -U pip
pip install -e ".[dev]"        # installs tessrax + dev extras
# Optional: pre-commit hooks for lint/format
pre-commit install

	3.	Run test suite

pytest -q
# Coverage gate: 85% minimum for changed code
pytest --cov=tessrax --cov-report=term-missing

	4.	Type-check & lint (CI parity)

mypy tessrax
ruff check .
ruff format .
bandit -r tessrax      # security scan
pip-audit              # dependency vuln audit

	5.	Run demo / UI

python tessrax/demo_flow.py
python tessrax/current.py     # launches API + dashboard


â¸»

ðŸŒ¿ Branching Model
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â main â€” protected; stable, tagged releases only.
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â develop â€” integration branch for completed features.
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â feature/<slug> â€” scoped feature work (small, iterative PRs).
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â fix/<slug> â€” scoped bugfix work.
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â release/<version> â€” pre-release hardening.

Keep branches short-lived; rebase onto develop before PR.

â¸»

ðŸ“ Commit Convention

Use Conventional Commits for traceable history and auto-changelogs:

feat(core): add scar severity indexing
fix(rigor/charity): resolve scope partition bug
docs(readme): clarify federation notes
refactor(ledger): simplify merkle root calc
test(governance): add quorum threshold cases
perf(semantic): cache normalized entities
chore(ci): pin mypy version

Include an imperative subject, optional scope, and concise body with rationale, links to issues, and BREAKING CHANGE notes if relevant.

â¸»

ðŸ” Pull Requests

Target: develop

Checklist (required):
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Tests added/updated; suite passes locally (pytest -q)
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Lint/format/type-check pass (ruff, mypy, pre-commit)
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Coverage â‰¥ 85% on changed lines (CI enforces)
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Docs updated (module docstrings and /docs where applicable)
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â No secrets or PII in code, tests, or fixtures
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â For governance-sensitive changes: updated charter/ or compliance/ as needed and included a short governance note in PR description
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Ledger-affecting logic includes receipt/merkle test vectors

How to PR
	1.	Fork â†’ create feature/<slug>
	2.	Commit using Conventional Commits
	3.	Rebase on develop (no merge commits if possible)
	4.	Open PR to develop with:
Â Â Â Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â What changed & why
Â Â Â Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Risks / rollback plan
Â Â Â Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Any migration steps
Â Â Â Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Screenshots (UI) or sample receipts (ledger)

Reviews
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â One maintainer approval minimum; two for governance/ledger-critical areas.
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â â€œChanges requestedâ€ pauses merge until addressed.
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â CI must be fully green.

â¸»

ðŸ§ª Testing Standards
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Unit tests (tests/unit/): pure logic, fast (<200ms each)
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Integration (tests/integration/): API, ledger, receipts, sandbox
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Rigor Layer (tests/rigor/): Hierarchy, Telos, Charity, Observer, Invariants, Multi-Scale
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Golden vectors for receipts/merkle under tests/data/
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Use pytest fixtures; avoid network access; use temporary FS.
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Deterministic seeds for stochastic pieces.

Coverage Policy
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â New modules: â‰¥90% lines; changed lines: â‰¥85%.
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Core crypto/ledger paths: 100% on happy-path + failure-path.

â¸»

ðŸ§­ Code Standards
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Python 3.11+; PEP 8/257 aligned via ruff + ruff format
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Type hints required (mypy --strict clean for new/changed modules)
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Public functions must have docstrings with brief examples
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Avoid global state; prefer pure functions and explicit deps
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Keep functions short; extract helpers rather than nesting deeply
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Errors: raise precise exceptions; include remediation hints

Modules of Interest
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â tessrax/core/ â€” contradiction detection, metabolism orchestration
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â tessrax/rigor/ â€” integrity band modules (Hierarchy, Telos, Charity, Observer, Invariants, Multi-Scale)
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â tessrax/ledger/ â€” append-only JSONL + Merkle root anchoring
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â tessrax/receipts/ â€” tamper-evident receipts & signatures
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â tessrax/dashboard/ â€” Flask/D3 audit views

â¸»

ðŸ” Security & Compliance
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â No secrets/PII in repo, tests, or logs. Use .env locally and mock secrets in tests.
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Run bandit, pip-audit before PR.
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Ledger files may contain hashes and non-sensitive metadata only.
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Changes to charter/quorum/revocation require a governance note and additional reviewer.

Responsible Disclosure (Security)
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Email: security@tessrax.example (placeholder)
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Do not open public issues for 0-days; weâ€™ll coordinate a fix and release.

ðŸ§­ Design Guardrails (Rigor Layer)

Before you mark any conflict a â€œcontradiction,â€ apply:
	1.	Principle of Charity â€” normalize terms, align scopes, check definitions.
	2.	Observer Relativity â€” verify itâ€™s not an artifact of models/instruments.
	3.	Equilibria & Invariants â€” allow lawful static truths and conserved relations.
	4.	Multi-Scale â€” translate to shared scale; avoid category errors.
	5.	Hierarchy of Differences â€” benign variety â‰  contradiction; escalate only when required.

These are enforced in code under tessrax/rigor/ and must be respected by new features.

a. Contradiction Delta Index (CDI)

Thermodynamic model for social entropy in hiring systems.

Variables
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Î”â‚ = 100 âˆ’ Response Rateâ€ƒ(Human Contact Loss)
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Î”â‚‚ = AI_Screening âˆ’ Human_Reviewâ€ƒ(Automation Burden)
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Î”â‚ƒ = Salary_Transparency âˆ’ Ghost_Jobsâ€ƒ(Transparency Recovery)

Formula

CDI = (Î”â‚ + Î”â‚‚ - Î”â‚ƒ) / 3

Interpretation
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â High CDI â†’ entropy dominates (system dehumanized)
Â Â Â â€¢Â Â Â Low CDI â†’ recovery exceeds entropy (system humane)

0â€“30	ðŸŸ¢ Functional	Equilibrium
31â€“45	ðŸŸ¡ Marginal	Manageable strain
46â€“60	ðŸŸ  Dysfunctional	Efficiency > empathy
>60	ðŸ”´ Critical	Systemic breakdown

import json, glob
data = []
for f in glob.glob("data/HRI/*.json"):
    with open(f) as file:
        data.append(json.load(file))
with open("data/HRI_Data_Lake_2025.jsonl","w") as out:
    for record in data:

b. CDI Calculator

def calc_cdi(response_rate, ai_screen, human_review, salary_trans, ghost_jobs):
    delta1 = 100 - response_rate
    delta2 = ai_screen - human_review
    delta3 = salary_trans - ghost_jobs
    return (delta1 + delta2 - delta3) / 3

c. Ledger Integration

from hashlib import sha256
def log_to_ledger(record):
    payload = json.dumps(record, sort_keys=True)
    h = sha256(payload.encode()).hexdigest()
    with open("Ledger.txt","a") as f:
        f.write(f"{h} :: {payload}\n")

# Tessrax-Core

**A contradiction-driven governance prototype. Where disagreement becomes data.**

Tessrax-Core is a minimal open prototype of a **contradiction-driven governance system** for multi-agent AI coordination.

## What It Does

It demonstrates:
- **Multi-agent contradiction detection** (CE-MOD-66)
- **Governance routing** (autonomic / deliberative / constitutional / audit)
- **Stability scoring and visualization**

The goal: show how disagreement between AIs can be used to **measure epistemic stability** and guide rule formation.

## Quick Start

```bash
# Setup
chmod +x setup.sh
./setup.sh
source .venv/bin/activate

# Run demo
python governance_kernel.py

# Visualize
python visualize_scaffolding.py
```

## Architecture

```
Agent Claims â†’ CE-MOD-66 â†’ Contradiction Graph â†’ Governance Kernel â†’ Ledger
```

See `docs/architecture_overview.md` for technical details.

## Philosophy

Traditional AI systems try to eliminate disagreement. Tessrax treats contradiction as **signal**â€”a measurement of where knowledge, values, or definitions are unstable.

When multiple AIs disagree:

- **Low contradiction** (S > 0.9) â†’ Safe to auto-adopt
- **Medium contradiction** (0.7-0.9) â†’ Needs human deliberation
- **High contradiction** (0.5-0.7) â†’ Constitutional drift; amend rules
- **Extreme contradiction** (< 0.5) â†’ Behavioral audit; check for manipulation

## File: `ce_mod_66.py`

```python
"""
CE-MOD-66 â€” Contradiction Graph Engine (public build)

Builds a graph of agent claims and detects contradictions.
Computes stability index: S = 1 - (contradictions / total_edges)
"""
import json
import itertools
import networkx as nx


def detect_contradictions(agent_claims):
    """
    Build contradiction graph from a list of {agent, claim, type}.
    
    Args:
        agent_claims: List of dicts with keys 'agent', 'claim', 'type'
    
    Returns:
        NetworkX Graph with contradiction edges
    """
    G = nx.Graph()
    
    for a in agent_claims:
        G.add_node(a["agent"], claim=a["claim"], ctype=a["type"])
    
    for a, b in itertools.combinations(agent_claims, 2):
        if a["claim"] != b["claim"]:
            G.add_edge(a["agent"], b["agent"], contradiction=True)
        else:
            G.add_edge(a["agent"], b["agent"], contradiction=False)
    
    return G


def score_stability(G):
    """
    Calculate stability index for a contradiction graph.
    
    S = 1 - (contradictory_edges / total_edges)
    
    Returns:
        Float between 0 (total disagreement) and 1 (total consensus)
    """
    total_edges = len(G.edges)
    if total_edges == 0:
        return 1.0
    
    contradictions = sum(1 for _, _, d in G.edges(data=True) if d.get("contradiction"))
    return 1 - (contradictions / total_edges)


if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Demo run
    with open("data/sample_agent_runs.json") as f:
        runs = json.load(f)
    
    G = detect_contradictions(runs)
    stability = score_stability(G)
    
    print(f"ðŸ“Š Contradiction Analysis:")
    print(f"   Agents: {len(G.nodes)}")
    print(f"   Edges: {len(G.edges)}")
    print(f"   Stability Index: {stability:.2f}")
```

## File: `governance_kernel.py`

```python
"""
Governance Kernel â€” routes contradictions into lanes

Lanes:
  - Autonomic: S > 0.9 (safe to auto-adopt)
  - Deliberative: 0.7 < S â‰¤ 0.9 (needs human review)
  - Constitutional: 0.5 < S â‰¤ 0.7 (rules drifting)
  - Behavioral Audit: S â‰¤ 0.5 (possible manipulation)
"""
import json
from ce_mod_66 import detect_contradictions, score_stability


def route(G):
    """
    Route a contradiction graph into governance lane.
    
    Returns:
        Dict with stability score and assigned lane
    """
    stability = score_stability(G)
    
    if stability > 0.9:
        lane = "autonomic"
    elif stability > 0.7:
        lane = "deliberative"
    elif stability > 0.5:
        lane = "constitutional"
    else:
        lane = "behavioral_audit"
    
    return {
        "stability": round(stability, 3),
        "lane": lane
    }


if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Demo run
    with open("data/sample_agent_runs.json") as f:
        runs = json.load(f)
    
    G = detect_contradictions(runs)
    result = route(G)
    
    print(f"ðŸŽ¯ Governance Routing:")
    print(f"   Stability: {result['stability']}")
    print(f"   Lane: {result['lane'].upper()}")
    print()
    
    # Explain the routing
    lane_descriptions = {
        "autonomic": "High consensusâ€”safe to auto-adopt",
        "deliberative": "Moderate conflictâ€”needs human quorum",
        "constitutional": "High conflictâ€”rule drift detected",
        "behavioral_audit": "Extreme conflictâ€”check for manipulation"
    }
    
    print(f"   Interpretation: {lane_descriptions[result['lane']]}")
```

## File: `visualize_scaffolding.py`

```python
"""
Quick visualizer for contradiction graphs.

Renders nodes (agents) and edges (contradictions) using NetworkX.
Red edges = contradiction, gray edges = agreement.
"""
import json
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import networkx as nx
from ce_mod_66 import detect_contradictions


def visualize(agent_claims, title="Contradiction Graph"):
    """
    Visualize agent contradiction graph.
    
    Args:
        agent_claims: List of agent claim dicts
        title: Graph title
    """
    G = detect_contradictions(agent_claims)
    
    # Layout
    pos = nx.spring_layout(G, seed=42)
    
    # Color edges by contradiction
    edge_colors = ["red" if d.get("contradiction") else "gray" 
                   for _, _, d in G.edges(data=True)]
    
    # Draw
    plt.figure(figsize=(10, 8))
    nx.draw(
        G, pos,
        with_labels=True,
        edge_color=edge_colors,
        node_color="#B0E0E6",
        node_size=1500,
        font_size=10,
        font_weight="bold",
        width=2
    )
    
    plt.title(title, fontsize=16, fontweight="bold")
    plt.tight_layout()
    plt.show()


if __name__ == "__main__":
    with open("data/sample_agent_runs.json") as f:
        runs = json.load(f)
    
    print("ðŸ” Visualizing contradiction graph...")
    visualize(runs, title="Sample Agent Claims: Contradiction Analysis")
```

## File: `docs/architecture_overview.md`

```markdown
# Tessrax-Core Architecture Overview

Tessrax-Core demonstrates how multi-agent contradiction analysis can become a
governance mechanism. It's a lightweight version of the full Tessrax stack.

---

## Core Modules

### CE-MOD-66 (`ce_mod_66.py`)
Builds the contradiction graph and computes a **stability index (S)**.

- **Nodes:** agent identities
- **Edges:** contradictions between claims
- **Edge attribute:** `contradiction=True/False`

The stability index is defined as:
```

S = 1 - (contradictory_edges / total_edges)

```
Where:
- S = 1.0 â†’ Perfect consensus
- S = 0.5 â†’ Half the agents disagree
- S = 0.0 â†’ Total disagreement

### Governance Kernel (`governance_kernel.py`)
Routes the current contradiction graph into one of four governance lanes:

| Lane | Stability Range | Description |
|------|-----------------|-------------|
| Autonomic | S > 0.9 | High consensus; safe to auto-adopt |
| Deliberative | 0.7 < S â‰¤ 0.9 | Needs structured human review |
| Constitutional | 0.5 < S â‰¤ 0.7 | Rules drifting; amend definitions |
| Behavioral Audit | S â‰¤ 0.5 | Possible bias or manipulation |

Each evaluation produces a JSON receipt for the ledger.

### Visualize Scaffolding (`visualize_scaffolding.py`)
Renders the contradiction graph using **NetworkX** and **Matplotlib**.

- Red edges indicate contradiction
- Gray edges indicate agreement
- Node layout shows consensus clusters

---

## Data Flow
```

agent_runs.json â†’ CE-MOD-66 â†’ Governance Kernel â†’ Ledger
â†“
Contradiction Graph
â†“
Visualization

```
Each step is auditable; the outputs can be version-controlled as research data.

---

## Extending Tessrax-Core

### Add New Agent Claims
Replace `data/sample_agent_runs.json` with new claim sets:

```json
[
  {"agent": "NewModel", "claim": "Your claim here", "type": "epistemic"}
]
```

### Add Contradiction Types

Extend `ce_mod_66.py` to detect:

- Temporal contradictions (ordering conflicts)
- Semantic contradictions (same word, different meaning)
- Normative contradictions (value conflicts)

### Log to Ledger

Append results to `ledger/example_ledger.jsonl`:

```python
import json
from datetime import datetime

result = route(G)
log_entry = {
    "timestamp": datetime.utcnow().isoformat() + "Z",
    "stability_index": result["stability"],
    "governance_lane": result["lane"],
    "note": "Your description here"
}

with open("ledger/example_ledger.jsonl", "a") as f:
    f.write(json.dumps(log_entry) + "\n")
```

### Visualize History

Plot stability over time:

```python
import json
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

with open("ledger/example_ledger.jsonl") as f:
    logs = [json.loads(line) for line in f]

timestamps = [log["timestamp"] for log in logs]
stability = [log["stability_index"] for log in logs]

plt.plot(timestamps, stability)
plt.ylabel("Stability Index")
plt.xlabel("Time")
plt.title("Stability Drift Over Time")
plt.show()
```

## Theoretical Foundation

Tessrax-Core operationalizes several key concepts:

### 1. Contradiction as Measurement

Instead of treating disagreement as error, we treat it as **data about epistemic state**.

### 2. Governance Without Adjudication

The system doesnâ€™t pick winnersâ€”it routes conflicts to appropriate resolution mechanisms.

### 3. Metabolic Learning

Amendments are tested for their effect on system stability. Good rules increase coherence; bad rules are reverted.

### 4. Institutional Memory

The ledger creates a case law of contradictionsâ€”showing which conflicts were resolved and how.

-----

## Research Applications

- **AI Safety**: Detect value drift in deployed systems
- **Policy Testing**: Stress-test governance documents against multi-agent interpretation
- **Truth Maintenance**: Track factual drift across model versions
- **Coordination**: Enable multi-agent systems to self-regulate

-----

## Limitations

This is a **minimal prototype**. The full Tessrax system includes:

- Semantic conflict detection (not just exact string matching)
- Weighted agent reliability scores
- Human deliberation protocols
- Constitutional amendment mechanisms
- Adversarial resistance testing

"""

â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
Complete production framework implementing:
- All primitives (ingest, classify, summarize, template, schedule)
- Config validation schemas
- Review dashboard for human approval
- Error recovery and retry logic
- Automated testing infrastructure (pytest-ready)

Integrates with existing Tessrax governance (audit trail, safety, and provenance).
"""

import json
import yaml

import logging
import threading

from dataclasses import dataclass, asdict
from pathlib import Path

from flask import Flask, request, render_template_string, redirect, url_for

import time

# â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
# LOGGING SETUP
# â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€
